<div class="noprint" id="mw-head-base">\n  </div>\n  <div class="mw-body" id="content" role="main">\n   <a id="top">\n   </a>\n   <div class="mw-body-content" id="siteNotice">\n    <!-- CentralNotice -->\n   </div>\n   <div class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n   </div>\n   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">\n    Rocket engine\n   </h1>\n   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">\n    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">\n     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia\n    </div>\n    <div id="contentSub">\n    </div>\n    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">\n     Jump to:\n     <a href="#mw-head">\n      navigation\n     </a>\n     ,\n     <a href="#p-search">\n      search\n     </a>\n    </div>\n    <div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en">\n     <div class="mw-parser-output">\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       This article is about a type of reaction engine. For rocket-propelled vehicles, see\n       <a href="/wiki/Rocket" title="Rocket">\n        Rocket\n       </a>\n       . For reaction engines not possessing a de Laval nozzle, see\n       <a href="/wiki/Reaction_engine" title="Reaction engine">\n        Reaction engine\n       </a>\n       .\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RS-68_rocket_engine_test.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="750" data-file-width="600" height="275" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/RS-68_rocket_engine_test.jpg/220px-RS-68_rocket_engine_test.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/RS-68_rocket_engine_test.jpg/330px-RS-68_rocket_engine_test.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/RS-68_rocket_engine_test.jpg/440px-RS-68_rocket_engine_test.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RS-68_rocket_engine_test.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/RS-68" title="RS-68">\n          RS-68\n         </a>\n         being tested at NASA\'s Stennis Space Center. The nearly transparent exhaust is due to this engine\'s exhaust being mostly\n         <a href="/wiki/Superheated_steam" title="Superheated steam">\n          superheated steam\n         </a>\n         (water vapour from its propellants, hydrogen and oxygen)\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Viking_5C_rocketengine.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3504" data-file-width="2336" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Viking_5C_rocketengine.jpg/220px-Viking_5C_rocketengine.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Viking_5C_rocketengine.jpg/330px-Viking_5C_rocketengine.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Viking_5C_rocketengine.jpg/440px-Viking_5C_rocketengine.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Viking_5C_rocketengine.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Viking_(rocket_engine)" title="Viking (rocket engine)">\n          Viking 5C rocket engine\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       A\n       <b>\n        rocket engine\n       </b>\n       is a type of\n       <a href="/wiki/Jet_engine" title="Jet engine">\n        jet engine\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       that uses only stored\n       <a href="/wiki/Rocket_propellant" title="Rocket propellant">\n        rocket propellant\n       </a>\n       mass for forming its high-speed propulsive\n       <a href="/wiki/Jet_(fluid)" title="Jet (fluid)">\n        jet\n       </a>\n       . Rocket engines are\n       <a href="/wiki/Reaction_engine" title="Reaction engine">\n        reaction engines\n       </a>\n       , obtaining thrust in accordance with\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newton%27s_third_law" title="Newton\'s third law">\n        Newton\'s third law\n       </a>\n       . Most rocket engines are\n       <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">\n        internal combustion engines\n       </a>\n       , although non-combusting forms (such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Cold_gas_thruster" title="Cold gas thruster">\n        cold gas thrusters\n       </a>\n       ) also exist. Vehicles propelled by rocket engines are commonly called\n       <a href="/wiki/Rocket" title="Rocket">\n        rockets\n       </a>\n       . Since they need no external material to form their jet, rocket engines can perform in a\n       <a href="/wiki/Vacuum" title="Vacuum">\n        vacuum\n       </a>\n       and thus can be used to propel\n       <a href="/wiki/Spacecraft" title="Spacecraft">\n        spacecraft\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Ballistic_missile" title="Ballistic missile">\n        ballistic missiles\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Compared to other types of jet engines, rocket engines are by far the lightest, and have the highest thrust, but are the least propellant-efficient (they have the lowest\n       <a href="/wiki/Specific_impulse" title="Specific impulse">\n        specific impulse\n       </a>\n       ). The ideal exhaust is\n       <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen" title="Hydrogen">\n        hydrogen\n       </a>\n       , the lightest of all gases, but chemical rockets produce a mix of heavier species, reducing the exhaust velocity. Rocket engines become more efficient at high velocities, due to greater\n       <a href="/wiki/Propulsive_efficiency" title="Propulsive efficiency">\n        propulsive efficiency\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Oberth_effect" title="Oberth effect">\n        Oberth effect\n       </a>\n       . Since they do not require an atmosphere, they are well suited for uses at very high altitudes and in space.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div   <span class="tocnumber">\n           13\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           History of rocket engines\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-43">\n         <a href="#See_also">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           14\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           See also\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-44">\n         <a href="#References">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           15\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           References\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-45">\n         <a href="#External_links">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           16\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Terminology">\n        Terminology\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rocket_engine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Terminology">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Here, "rocket" is used as an abbreviation for "rocket engine".\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        <a href="/wiki/Thermal_rocket" title="Thermal rocket">\n         Thermal rockets\n        </a>\n       </b>\n       use an inert propellant, heated by a power source such as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electrothermal_propulsion" title="Electrothermal propulsion">\n        electric\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_thermal_rocket" title="Nuclear thermal rocket">\n        nuclear power\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        Chemical rockets\n       </b>\n       are powered by\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exothermic" title="Exothermic">\n        exothermic\n       </a>\n       chemical reactions of the propellant:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solid-fuel_rocket" title="Solid-fuel rocket">\n          Solid-fuel rockets\n         </a>\n        </b>\n        (or\n        <b>\n         solid-propellant rockets\n        </b>\n        or\n        <b>\n         motors\n        </b>\n        ) are chemical rockets which use propellant in a solid state.\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         <a href="/wiki/Liquid-propellant_rocket" title="Liquid-propellant rocket">\n          Liquid-propellant rockets\n         </a>\n        </b>\n        use one or more liquid propellants fed from tanks.\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hybrid_rocket" title="Hybrid rocket">\n          Hybrid rockets\n         </a>\n        </b>\n        use a solid propellant in the combustion chamber, to which a second liquid or gas\n        <a href="/wiki/Oxidizing_agent" title="Oxidizing agent">\n         oxidiser\n        </a>\n        or propellant is added to permit combustion.\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         <a href="/wiki/Monopropellant_rocket" title="Monopropellant rocket">\n          Monopropellant rockets\n         </a>\n        </b>\n        use a single propellant decomposed by a\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catalyst" title="Catalyst">\n         catalyst\n        </a>\n        . The most common monopropellants are\n        <a href="/wiki/Hydrazine" title="Hydrazine">\n         hydrazine\n        </a>\n        and\n        <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_peroxide" title="Hydrogen peroxide">\n         hydrogen peroxide\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Principle_of_operation">\n        Principle of operation\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rocket_engine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Principle of operation">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Rocket engines produce thrust by the expulsion of an exhaust\n       <a href="/wiki/Fluid" title="Fluid">\n        fluid\n       </a>\n       which has been accelerated to a high speed through a\n       <a href="/wiki/Propelling_nozzle" title="Propelling nozzle">\n        propelling nozzle\n       </a>\n       . The fluid is usually a gas created by high pressure (150-to-2,900-pound-per-square-inch (10 to 200\xc2\xa0bar)) combustion of solid or liquid\n       <a href="/wiki/Rocket_propellant" title="Rocket propellant">\n        propellants\n       </a>\n       , consisting of\n       <a href="/wiki/Fuel" title="Fuel">\n        fuel\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Oxidizing_agent" title="Oxidizing agent">\n        oxidiser\n       </a>\n       components, within a\n       <a href="/wiki/Combustion_chamber" title="Combustion chamber">\n        combustion chamber\n       </a>\n       . The nozzle uses the heat energy released by expansion of the gas to accelerate the exhaust to very high (\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Supersonic" title="Supersonic">\n        supersonic\n       </a>\n       ) speed, and the reaction to this pushes the engine in the opposite direction. Combustion is most frequently used for practical rockets, as high temperatures and pressures are desirable for the best performance, permitting a longer nozzle, giving higher exhaust speeds and better thermodynamic efficiency.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       An alternative to combustion is the\n       <a href="/wiki/Water_rocket" title="Water rocket">\n        water rocket\n       </a>\n       , which uses water pressurised by compressed air,\n       <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">\n        carbon dioxide\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen" title="Nitrogen">\n        nitrogen\n       </a>\n       , or manual pumping, for\n       <a href="/wiki/Model_rocket" title="Model rocket">\n        model rocketry\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Propellant">\n        Propellant\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rocket_engine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Propellant">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Rocket propellant is mass that is stored, usually in some form of propellant tank, or within the combustion chamber itself, prior to being ejected from a rocket engine in the form of a fluid jet to produce thrust.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Chemical rocket propellants are most commonly used, which undergo exothermic chemical reactions which produce hot gas which is used by a rocket for propulsive purposes. Alternatively, a chemically inert\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reaction_mass" title="Reaction mass">\n        reaction mass\n       </a>\n       can be heated using a high-energy power source via a heat exchanger, and then no combustion chamber is used.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SolidRocketMotor.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="338" data-file-width="504" height="201" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/SolidRocketMotor.svg/300px-SolidRocketMotor.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/SolidRocketMotor.svg/450px-SolidRocketMotor.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/SolidRocketMotor.svg/600px-SolidRocketMotor.svg.png 2x" width="300"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SolidRocketMotor.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A solid rocket motor.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solid_rocket" title="Solid rocket">\n        Solid rocket\n       </a>\n       propellants are prepared as a mixture of fuel and oxidising components called \'grain\' and the propellant storage casing effectively becomes the combustion chamber.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Injection">\n        Injection\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rocket_engine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Injection">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liquid_rocket" title="Liquid rocket">\n        Liquid-fuelled rockets\n       </a>\n       force separate fuel and oxidiser components into the combustion chamber, where they mix and burn.\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hybrid_rocket" title="Hybrid rocket">\n        Hybrid rocket\n       </a>\n       engines use a combination of solid and liquid or gaseous propellants. Both liquid and hybrid rockets use\n       <i>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liquid-fuel_rocket#Injectors" title="Liquid-fuel rocket">\n         injectors\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       to introduce the propellant into the chamber. These are often an array of simple\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jet_(nozzle)" title="Jet (nozzle)">\n        jets\n       </a>\n       - holes through which the propellant escapes under pressure; but sometimes may be more complex spray nozzles. When two or more propellants are injected, the jets usually deliberately cause the propellants to collide as this breaks up the flow into smaller droplets that burn more easily.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Combustion_chamber">\n        Combustion chamber\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rocket_engine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Combustion chamber">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Combustion_chamber" title="Combustion chamber">\n        Combustion chamber\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       For chemical rockets the combustion chamber is typically just a cylinder, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Flame_holder" title="Flame holder">\n        flame holders\n       </a>\n       are rarely used. The dimensions of the cylinder are such that the propellant is able to combust thoroughly; different\n       <a href="/wiki/Rocket_propellant" title="Rocket propellant">\n        rocket propellants\n       </a>\n       require different combustion chamber sizes for this to occur. This leads to a number called\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <msup>\n              <mi>\n               L\n              </mi>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mo>\n                \xe2\x88\x97\n                <!-- \xe2\x88\x97 -->\n               </mo>\n              </mrow>\n             </msup>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle L^{*}}\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="L^{*}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d9a3547ba2f3cc5cb4463473815f227092b4766a" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.655ex; height:2.343ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       :\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <msup>\n               <mi>\n                L\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mo>\n                 \xe2\x88\x97\n                 <!-- \xe2\x88\x97 -->\n                </mo>\n               </mrow>\n              </msup>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mfrac>\n                <msub>\n                 <mi>\n                  V\n                 </mi>\n                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                  <mi>\n                   c\n                  </mi>\n                 </mrow>\n                </msub>\n                <msub>\n                 <mi>\n                  A\n                 </mi>\n                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                  <mi>\n                   t\n                  </mi>\n                 </mrow>\n                </msub>\n               </mfrac>\n              </mrow>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle L^{*}={\\frac {V_{c}}{A_{t}}}}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="L^{*}={\\frac {V_{c}}{A_{t}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ebda5f41ab782518ce17a3572a47fc8cee879cc7" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:9.187ex; height:5.843ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       where:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                V\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mi>\n                 c\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle V_{c}}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="V_{c}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/338b595db7a169754c5e088d9881010c2225f597" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.317ex; height:2.509ex;"/>\n        </span>\n        is the volume of the chamber\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                A\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mi>\n                 t\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle A_{t}}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="A_{t}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/265483c517cb98cde609f03a31964d86cdcb05c9" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.587ex; height:2.676ex;"/>\n        </span>\n        is the area of the throat\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       L* is typically in the range of 25\xe2\x80\x9360 inches (0.64\xe2\x80\x931.52\xc2\xa0m).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The combination of temperatures and pressures typically reached in a combustion chamber is usually extreme by any standards. Unlike in\n       <a href="/wiki/Airbreathing_jet_engine" title="Airbreathing jet engine">\n        airbreathing jet engines\n       </a>\n       , no atmospheric nitrogen is present to dilute and cool the combustion, and the temperature can reach true\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stoichiometric" title="Stoichiometric">\n        stoichiometric\n       </a>\n       ratios. This, in combination with the high pressures, means that the rate of heat conduction through the walls is very high.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Nozzle">\n        Nozzle\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rocket_engine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Nozzle">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Rocket_engine_nozzle" title="Rocket engine nozzle">\n        Rocket engine nozzle\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rocket_thrust.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="247" data-file-width="768" height="71" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Rocket_thrust.svg/220px-Rocket_thrust.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Rocket_thrust.svg/330px-Rocket_thrust.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Rocket_thrust.svg/440px-Rocket_thrust.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rocket_thrust.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Rocket thrust is caused by pressures acting in the combustion chamber and nozzle. From Newton\'s third law, equal and opposite pressures act on the exhaust, and this accelerates it to high speeds.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The hot gas produced in the combustion chamber is permitted to escape through an opening (the "throat"), and then through a diverging expansion section. When sufficient pressure is provided to the nozzle (about 2.5-3 times ambient pressure), the nozzle\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Choked_flow" title="Choked flow">\n         chokes\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       and a supersonic jet is formed, dramatically accelerating the gas, converting most of the thermal energy into kinetic energy. Exhaust speeds vary, depending on the expansion ratio the nozzle is designed for, but exhaust speeds as high as ten times the\n       <a href="/wiki/Speed_of_sound" title="Speed of sound">\n        speed of sound\n       </a>\n       in air at sea level are not uncommon. About half of the rocket engine\'s thrust comes from the unbalanced pressures inside the combustion chamber, and the rest comes from the pressures acting against the inside of the nozzle (see diagram). As the gas expands (\n       <a href="/wiki/Adiabatic_process" title="Adiabatic process">\n        adiabatically\n       </a>\n       ) the pressure against the nozzle\'s walls forces the rocket engine in one direction while accelerating the gas in the other.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <span id="opt_expansion">\n       </span>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rocket_nozzle_expansion.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1132" data-file-width="599" height="321" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Rocket_nozzle_expansion.svg/170px-Rocket_nozzle_expansion.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Rocket_nozzle_expansion.svg/255px-Rocket_nozzle_expansion.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Rocket_nozzle_expansion.svg/340px-Rocket_nozzle_expansion.svg.png 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rocket_nozzle_expansion.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The four expansion regimes of a de Laval nozzle:\n         <br/>\n         \xe2\x80\xa2 underexpanded\n         <br/>\n         \xe2\x80\xa2 perfectly expanded\n         <br/>\n         \xe2\x80\xa2 overexpanded\n         <br/>\n         \xe2\x80\xa2 grossly overexpanded\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The most commonly used nozzle is the\n       <a href="/wiki/De_Laval_nozzle" title="De Laval nozzle">\n        de Laval nozzle\n       </a>\n       , a fixed geometry nozzle with a high expansion-ratio. The large bell- or cone-shaped nozzle extension beyond the throat gives the rocket engine its characteristic shape.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The exit\n       <a href="/wiki/Static_pressure#Static_pressure_in_fluid_dynamics" title="Static pressure">\n        static pressure\n       </a>\n       of the exhaust jet depends on the chamber pressure and the ratio of exit to throat area of the nozzle. As exit pressure varies from the ambient (atmospheric) pressure, a choked nozzle is said to be\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         underexpanded\n        </b>\n        (exit pressure greater than ambient),\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         perfectly expanded\n        </b>\n        (exit pressure equals ambient),\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         overexpanded\n        </b>\n        (exit pressure less than ambient;\n        <a href="/wiki/Shock_diamond" title="Shock diamond">\n         shock diamonds\n        </a>\n        form outside the nozzle), or\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         grossly overexpanded\n        </b>\n        (a\n        <a href="/wiki/Shock_wave" title="Shock wave">\n         shock wave\n        </a>\n        forms inside the nozzle extension). In practice, perfect expansion is only achievable with a variable-exit area nozzle (since ambient pressure decreases as altitude increases), and is not possible above a certain altitude as ambient pressure approaches zero. If the nozzle is not perfectly expanded, then loss of efficiency occurs. Grossly overexpanded nozzles lose less efficiency, but can cause mechanical problems with the nozzle. Fixed-area nozzles become progressively more underexpanded as they gain altitude. Almost all de Laval nozzles will be momentarily grossly overexpanded during startup in an atmosphere.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">\n         <a href="#cite_note-2">\n          [2]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       Nozzle efficiency is affected by operation in the atmosphere because atmospheric pressure changes with altitude; but due to the supersonic speeds of the gas exiting from a rocket engine, the pressure of the jet may be either below or above ambient, and equilibrium between the two is not reached at all altitudes (see diagram).\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Back_pressure_and_optimal_expansion">\n        Back pressure and optimal expansion\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rocket_engine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Back pressure and optimal expansion">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       For optimal performance the pressure of the gas at the end of the nozzle should just equal the ambient pressure: if the exhaust\'s pressure is lower than the ambient pressure, then the vehicle will be slowed by the difference in pressure between the top of the engine and the exit; on the other hand, if the exhaust\'s pressure is higher, then exhaust pressure that could have been converted into thrust is not converted, and energy is wasted.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       To maintain this ideal of equality between the exhaust\'s exit pressure and the ambient pressure, the diameter of the nozzle would need to increase with altitude, giving the pressure a longer nozzle to act on (and reducing the exit pressure and temperature). This increase is difficult to arrange in a lightweight fashion, although is routinely done with other forms of jet engines. In rocketry a lightweight compromise nozzle is generally used and some reduction in atmospheric performance occurs when used at other than the \'design altitude\' or when throttled. To improve on this, various exotic nozzle designs such as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Plug_nozzle" title="Plug nozzle">\n        plug nozzle\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stepped_nozzles" title="Stepped nozzles">\n        stepped nozzles\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Expanding_nozzle" title="Expanding nozzle">\n        expanding nozzle\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Aerospike_engine" title="Aerospike engine">\n        aerospike\n       </a>\n       have been proposed, each providing some way to adapt to changing ambient air pressure and each allowing the gas to expand further against the nozzle, giving extra thrust at higher altitudes.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       When exhausting into a sufficiently low ambient pressure (vacuum) several issues arise. One is the sheer weight of the nozzle\xe2\x80\x94beyond a certain point, for a particular vehicle, the extra weight of the nozzle outweighs any performance gained. Secondly, as the exhaust gases adiabatically expand within the nozzle they cool, and eventually some of the chemicals can freeze, producing \'snow\' within the jet. This causes instabilities in the jet and must be avoided.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On a\n       <a href="/wiki/De_Laval_nozzle" title="De Laval nozzle">\n        de Laval nozzle\n       </a>\n       , exhaust gas flow detachment will occur in a grossly over-expanded nozzle. As the detachment point will not be uniform around the axis of the engine, a side force may be imparted to the engine. This side force may change over time and result in control problems with the launch vehicle.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Advanced\n       <a href="/wiki/Altitude_compensating_nozzle" title="Altitude compensating nozzle">\n        altitude-compensating\n       </a>\n       designs, such as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Aerospike_engine" title="Aerospike engine">\n        aerospike\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a href="/wiki/Plug_nozzle" title="Plug nozzle">\n        plug nozzle\n       </a>\n       , attempt to minimize performance losses by adjusting to varying expansion ratio caused by changing altitude.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Propellant_efficiency">\n        Propellant efficiency\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rocket_engine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Propellant efficiency">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Specific_impulse" title="Specific impulse">\n        Specific impulse\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nozzle_de_Laval_diagram.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1101" data-file-width="836" height="224" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Nozzle_de_Laval_diagram.svg/170px-Nozzle_de_Laval_diagram.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Nozzle_de_Laval_diagram.svg/255px-Nozzle_de_Laval_diagram.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Nozzle_de_Laval_diagram.svg/340px-Nozzle_de_Laval_diagram.svg.png 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nozzle_de_Laval_diagram.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Typical temperature (T), pressure (p), and velocity (v) profiles in a de Laval Nozzle\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       For a rocket engine to be propellant efficient, it is important that the maximum pressures possible be created on the walls of the chamber and nozzle by a specific amount of propellant; as this is the source of the thrust. This can be achieved by all of:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        heating the propellant to as high a temperature as possible (using a high energy fuel, containing hydrogen and carbon and sometimes metals such as\n        <a href="/wiki/Aluminium" title="Aluminium">\n         aluminium\n        </a>\n        , or even using nuclear energy)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        using a low specific density gas (as hydrogen rich as possible)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        using propellants which are, or decompose to, simple molecules with few degrees of freedom to maximise translational velocity\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       Since all of these things minimise the mass of the propellant used, and since pressure is proportional to the mass of propellant present to be accelerated as it pushes on the engine, and since from\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newton%27s_third_law" title="Newton\'s third law">\n        Newton\'s third law\n       </a>\n       the pressure that acts on the engine also reciprocally acts on the propellant, it turns out that for any given engine, the speed that the propellant leaves the chamber is unaffected by the chamber pressure (although the thrust is proportional). However, speed is significantly affected by all three of the above factors and the exhaust speed is an excellent measure of the engine propellant efficiency. This is termed\n       <i>\n        exhaust velocity\n       </i>\n       , and after allowance is made for factors that can reduce it, the\n       <b>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Effective_exhaust_velocity" title="Effective exhaust velocity">\n         effective exhaust velocity\n        </a>\n       </b>\n       is one of the most important parameters of a rocket engine (although weight, cost, ease of manufacture etc. are usually also very important).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       For aerodynamic reasons the flow goes sonic ("\n       <a href="/wiki/Choked_flow" title="Choked flow">\n        chokes\n       </a>\n       ") at the narrowest part of the nozzle, the \'throat\'. Since the\n       <a href="/wiki/Speed_of_sound" title="Speed of sound">\n        speed of sound\n       </a>\n       in gases increases with the square root of temperature, the use of hot exhaust gas greatly improves performance. By comparison, at room temperature the speed of sound in air is about 340\xc2\xa0m/s while the speed of sound in the hot gas of a rocket engine can be over 1700\xc2\xa0m/s; much of this performance is due to the higher temperature, but additionally rocket propellants are chosen to be of low molecular mass, and this also gives a higher velocity compared to air.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Expansion in the rocket nozzle then further multiplies the speed, typically between 1.5 and 2 times, giving a highly\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Collimated" title="Collimated">\n        collimated\n       </a>\n       hypersonic exhaust jet. The speed increase of a rocket nozzle is mostly determined by its area expansion ratio\xe2\x80\x94the ratio of the area of the throat to the area at the exit, but detailed properties of the gas are also important. Larger ratio nozzles are more massive but are able to extract more heat from the combustion gases, increasing the exhaust velocity.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Thrust_vectoring">\n        Thrust vectoring\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rocket_engine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Thrust vectoring">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Thrust_vectoring" title="Thrust vectoring">\n        Thrust vectoring\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Vehicles typically require the overall thrust to change direction over the length of the burn. A number of different ways to achieve this have been flown:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        The entire engine is mounted on a\n        <a href="/wiki/Hinge" title="Hinge">\n         hinge\n        </a>\n        or\n        <a href="/wiki/Gimbal" title="Gimbal">\n         gimbal\n        </a>\n        and any propellant feeds reach the engine via low pressure flexible pipes or rotary couplings.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Just the combustion chamber and nozzle is gimballed, the pumps are fixed, and high pressure feeds attach to the engine.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Multiple engines (often canted at slight angles) are deployed but throttled to give the overall vector that is required, giving only a very small penalty.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        High-temperature vanes protrude into the exhaust and can be tilted to deflect the jet.\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Overall_performance">\n        Overall performance\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rocket_engine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Overall performance">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Rocket technology can combine very high thrust (\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Meganewton" title="Meganewton">\n        meganewtons\n       </a>\n       ), very high exhaust speeds (around 10 times the speed of sound in air at sea level) and very high thrust/weight ratios (&gt;100)\n       <i>\n        simultaneously\n       </i>\n       as well as being able to operate outside the atmosphere, and while permitting the use of low pressure and hence lightweight tanks and structure.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Rockets can be further optimised to even more extreme performance along one or more of these axes at the expense of the others.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Specific_impulse">\n        Specific impulse\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rocket_engine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Specific impulse">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Specific_impulse" title="Specific impulse">\n        Specific impulse\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center; float:right; clear:right; margin-left:1em">\n       <caption>\n        <a   <tr>\n        <th>\n         <a href="/wiki/S-IC" title="S-IC">\n          Saturn V\n          <br/>\n          stage 1\n         </a>\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Liquid_oxygen" title="Liquid oxygen">\n          LOX\n         </a>\n         /\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rocket_propellant-1" title="Rocket propellant-1">\n          RP-1\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         304\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spec_impulse_3-3">\n          <a href="#cite_note-spec_impulse-3">\n           [3]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       The most important metric for the efficiency of a rocket engine is\n       <a href="/wiki/Impulse_(physics)" title="Impulse (physics)">\n        impulse\n       </a>\n       per unit of\n       <a href="/wiki/Propellant" title="Propellant">\n        propellant\n       </a>\n       , this is called\n       <a href="/wiki/Specific_impulse" title="Specific impulse">\n        specific impulse\n       </a>\n       (usually written\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <msub>\n              <mi>\n               I\n              </mi>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mi>\n                s\n               </mi>\n               <mi>\n                p\n               </mi>\n              </mrow>\n             </msub>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle I_{sp}}\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="I_{sp}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1a1690436c8acf9d7a116f907128ad186af65815" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:2.879ex; height:2.843ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       ). This is either measured as a speed (the\n       <i>\n        effective exhaust velocity\n       </i>\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <msub>\n              <mi>\n               v\n              </mi>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mi>\n                e\n               </mi>\n              </mrow>\n             </msub>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle v_{e}}\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="v_{e}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3271a14c35fc1b6cb549d4d462e8d3255185cc9d" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.144ex; height:2.009ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       in metres/second or ft/s) or as a time (seconds). An engine that gives a large specific impulse is normally highly desirable.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The specific impulse that can be achieved is primarily a function of the propellant mix (and ultimately would limit the specific impulse), but practical limits on chamber pressures and the nozzle expansion ratios reduce the performance that can be achieved.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Net_thrust">\n        Net thrust\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n      </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Thrust" title="Thrust">\n        Thrust\n         </mi>\n                   <mi>\n                    t\n                   </mi>\n                  </mrow>\n                 </msub>\n                </mstyle>\n               </mrow>\n               <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n                {\\displaystyle v_{e-opt}}\n               </annotation>\n              </semantics>\n             </math>\n            </span>\n            <img alt="{\\displaystyle v_{e-opt}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a98d98485116a6d6587ae72f782f95d5b4ef0fb7" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:5.67ex; height:2.343ex;"/>\n           </span>\n          </th>\n          <td align="left">\n           =\xc2\xa0 effective jet velocity when Pa = Pe\n          </td>\n         </tr>\n         <tr>\n          <th align="right">\n           <span class="mwe-math-element">\n            <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n             <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n              <semantics>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n                 <msub>\n                  <mi>\n                   A\n                  </mi>\n                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                   <mi>\n                    e\n                   </mi>\n                  </mrow>\n                 </msub>\n                </mstyle>\n               </mrow>\n               <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n                {\\displaystyle A_{e}}\n               </annotation>\n              </semantics>\n             </math>\n            </span>\n            <img alt="A_{e}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/abcfbb3d2f9f962e32527c7037cdfa6e7da0e887" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.759ex; height:2.676ex;"/>\n           </span>\n          </th>\n          <td align="left">\n           =\xc2\xa0 flow area at nozzle exit plane (or the plane where the jet leaves the nozzle if separated flow)\n          </td>\n         </tr>\n         <tr>\n          <th align="right">\n           <span class="mwe-math-element">\n            <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n             <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n              <semantics>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n                 <msub>\n                  <mi>\n                   p\n                  </mi>\n                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                   <mi>\n                    e\n                   </mi>\n                  </mrow>\n                 </msub>\n                </mstyle>\n               </mrow>\n               <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n                {\\displaystyle p_{e}}\n               </annotation>\n              </semantics>\n             </math>\n            </span>\n            <img alt="p_{e}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ea9d1daea5e2e2bca1b08d45ef8f2b10a55184ea" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; margin-left: -0.079ex; width:2.265ex; height:2.009ex;"/>\n           </span>\n          </th>\n          <td align="left">\n           =\xc2\xa0 static pressure at nozzle exit plane\n          </td>\n         </tr>\n         <tr>\n          <th align="right">\n           <span class="mwe-math-element">\n            <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n             <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n              <semantics>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n                 <msub>\n                  <mi>\n                   p\n                  </mi>\n                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                   <mi>\n                    a\n                   </mi>\n                   <mi>\n                    m\n                   </mi>\n                   <mi>\n                    b\n                   </mi>\n                  </mrow>\n                 </msub>\n                </mstyle>\n               </mrow>\n               <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n                {\\displaystyle p_{amb}}\n               </annotation>\n              </semantics>\n             </math>\n            </span>\n            <img alt="p_{amb}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1637884c3ee70295587e32b9f1d9780ef7a1e512" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; margin-left: -0.079ex; width:4.531ex; height:2.009ex;"/>\n           </span>\n          </th>\n          <td align="left">\n           =\xc2\xa0 ambient (or atmospheric) pressure\n          </td>\n         </tr>\n        </table>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       Since, unlike a jet engine, a conventional rocket motor lacks an air intake, there is no \'ram drag\' to deduct from the gross thrust. Consequently, the net thrust of a rocket motor is equal to the gross thrust (apart from static back pressure).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mover>\n                <mi>\n                 m\n                </mi>\n                <mo>\n                 \xcb\x99\n                 <!-- \xcb\x99 -->\n                </mo>\n               </mover>\n              </mrow>\n             </mrow>\n             <mspace width="thickmathspace">\n             </mspace>\n             <msub>\n              <mi>\n               v\n              </mi>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mi>\n                e\n               </mi>\n               <mo>\n                \xe2\x88\x92\n                <!-- \xe2\x88\x92 -->\n               </mo>\n               <mi>\n                o\n               </mi>\n               <mi>\n                p\n               </mi>\n               <mi>\n                t\n               </mi>\n              </mrow>\n             </msub>\n             <mspace width="thinmathspace">\n             </mspace>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle {\\dot {m}}\\;v_{e-opt}\\,}\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="{\\displaystyle {\\dot {m}}\\;v_{e-opt}\\,}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/cc526befbf419fbcdba5f7d258309b02b78286c0" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:8.753ex; height:2.843ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       term represents the momentum thrust, which remains constant at a given throttle setting, whereas the\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <msub>\n              <mi>\n               A\n              </mi>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mi>\n                e\n               </mi>\n              </mrow>\n             </msub>\n             <mo stretchy="false">\n              (\n             </mo>\n             <msub>\n              <mi>\n               p\n              </mi>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mi>\n                e\n               </mi>\n              </mrow>\n             </msub>\n             <mo>\n              \xe2\x88\x92\n              <!-- \xe2\x88\x92 -->\n             </mo>\n             <msub>\n              <mi>\n               p\n              </mi>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mi>\n                a\n               </mi>\n               <mi>\n                m\n               </mi>\n               <mi>\n                b\n               </mi>\n              </mrow>\n             </msub>\n             <mo stretchy="false">\n              )\n             </mo>\n             <mspace width="thinmathspace">\n             </mspace>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle A_{e}(p_{e}-p_{amb})\\,}\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="A_{e}(p_{e}-p_{amb})\\," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/799a8f33c1257be36d3251c64e859b3e17738aa0" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:14.465ex; height:2.843ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       term represents the pressure thrust term. At full throttle, the net thrust of a rocket motor improves slightly with increasing altitude, because as atmospheric pressure decreases with altitude, the pressure thrust term increases. At the surface of the Earth the pressure thrust may be reduced by up to 30%,depending on the engine design. This reduction drops roughly exponentially to zero with increasing altitude.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Maximum efficiency for a rocket engine is achieved by maximising the momentum contribution of the equation without incurring penalties from over expanding the exhaust. This occurs when\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <msub>\n              <mi>\n               p\n              </mi>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mi>\n                e\n               </mi>\n              </mrow>\n             </msub>\n             <mo>\n              =\n             </mo>\n             <msub>\n              <mi>\n               p\n              </mi>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mi>\n                a\n               </mi>\n               <mi>\n                m\n               </mi>\n               <mi>\n                b\n               </mi>\n              </mrow>\n             </msub>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle p_{e}=p_{amb}}\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="p_{e}=p_{amb}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/191895155d9304c105bc21222789f50354dd53ba" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; margin-left: -0.079ex; width:9.826ex; height:2.009ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       . Since ambient pressure changes with altitude, most rocket engines spend very little time operating at peak efficiency.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Vacuum_Isp">\n        Vacuum I\n        <sub>\n         sp\n        </sub>\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rocket_engine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Vacuum Isp">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Due to the specific impulse varying with pressure, a quantity that is easy to compare and calculate with is useful. Because rockets\n       <a href="/wiki/Choked_flow" title="Choked flow">\n        choke\n       </a>\n       at the throat, and because the supersonic exhaust prevents external pressure influences travelling upstream, it turns out that the pressure at the exit is ideally exactly proportional to the propellant flow\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mover>\n                <mi>\n                 m\n                </mi>\n                <mo>\n                 \xcb\x99\n                 <!-- \xcb\x99 -->\n                </mo>\n               </mover>\n              </mrow>\n             </mrow>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle {\\dot {m}}}\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="{\\dot {m}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ad59b9876301e8fb75b9ddbf08de594b87251d3b" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.051ex; height:2.176ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       , provided the mixture ratios and combustion efficiencies are maintained. It is thus quite usual to rearrange the above equation slightly:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math      a\n                </mi>\n                <mi>\n                 c\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <mo>\n               =\n <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Throttling">\n        Throttling\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rocket_engine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Throttling">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Rockets can be throttled by controlling the propellant combustion rate\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mover>\n                <mi>\n                 m\n                </mi>\n                <mo>\n                 \xcb\x99\n                 <!-- \xcb\x99 -->\n                </mo>\n               </mover>\n              </mrow>\n             </mrow>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle {\\dot {m}}}\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="{\\dot {m}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ad59b9876301e8fb75b9ddbf08de594b87251d3b" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.051ex; height:2.176ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       (usually measured in kg/s or lb/s). In liquid and hybrid rockets, the propellant flow entering the chamber is controlled using valves, in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solid_rocket" title="Solid rocket">\n        solid rockets\n       </a>\n       it is controlled by changing the area of propellant that is burning and this can be designed into the propellant grain (and hence cannot be controlled in real-time).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Rockets can usually be throttled down to an exit pressure of about one-third of ambient pressure\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sutton_6-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Sutton-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       (often limited by flow separation in nozzles) and up to a maximum limit determined only by the mechanical strength of the engine.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In practice, the degree to which rockets can be throttled varies greatly, but most rockets can be throttled by a factor of 2 without great difficulty;\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sutton_6-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Sutton-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the typical limitation is combustion stability, as for example, injectors need a minimum pressure to avoid triggering damaging oscillations (chugging or combustion instabilities); but injectors can be optimised and tested for wider ranges. For example, some more recent liquid-propellant engine designs that have been optimised for greater throttling capability can be throttled to as low as 18\xe2\x80\x9320 percent of rated thrust.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sn20150407_7-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sn20150407-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sfi20160927_8-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sfi20160927-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Solid rockets can be throttled by using shaped grains that will vary their surface area over the course of the burn.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sutton_6-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Sutton-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Energy_efficiency">\n        Energy efficiency\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rocket_engine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Energy efficiency">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Further information:\n       <a href="/wiki/Rocket#Energy_efficiency" title="Rocket">\n        Rocket \xc2\xa7\xc2\xa0Energy efficiency\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rocket_propulsion_efficiency.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="512" data-file-width="512" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Rocket_propulsion_efficiency.svg/220px-Rocket_propulsion_efficiency.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Rocket_propulsion_efficiency.svg/330px-Rocket_propulsion_efficiency.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Rocket_propulsion_efficiency.svg/440px-Rocket_propulsion_efficiency.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rocket_propulsion_efficiency.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Rocket vehicle mechanical efficiency as a function of vehicle instantaneous speed divided by effective exhaust speed. These percentages need to be multiplied by internal engine efficiency to get overall efficiency.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Rocket engine nozzles are surprisingly efficient\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heat_engines" title="Heat engines">\n        heat engines\n       </a>\n       for generating a high speed jet, as a consequence of the high combustion temperature and high\n       <a href="/wiki/Compression_ratio" title="Compression ratio">\n        compression ratio\n       </a>\n       . Rocket nozzles give an excellent approximation to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adiabatic_expansion" title="Adiabatic expansion">\n        adiabatic expansion\n       </a>\n       which is a reversible process, and hence they give efficiencies which are very close to that of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Carnot_cycle" title="Carnot cycle">\n        Carnot cycle\n       </a>\n       . Given the temperatures reached, over 60% efficiency can be achieved with chemical rockets.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       For a\n       <i>\n        vehicle\n       </i>\n       employing a rocket engine the energetic efficiency is very good if the vehicle speed approaches or somewhat exceeds the exhaust velocity (relative to launch); but at low speeds the energy efficiency goes to 0% at zero speed (as with all\n       <a href="/wiki/Jet_propulsion" title="Jet propulsion">\n        jet propulsion\n       </a>\n       .) See\n       <a href="/wiki/Rocket#Energy_efficiency" title="Rocket">\n        Rocket energy efficiency\n       </a>\n       for more details.\n      </p>\n      <div style="clear:both;">\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Thrust-to-weight_ratio">\n        Thrust-to-weight ratio\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rocket_engine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Thrust-to-weight ratio">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Thrust-to-weight_ratio" title="Thrust-to-weight ratio">\n        thrust-to-weight ratio\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Rockets, of all the jet engines, indeed of essentially all engines, have the highest thrust to weight ratio. This is especially true for liquid rocket engines.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       This high performance is due to the small volume of\n       <a href="/wiki/Pressure_vessel" title="Pressure vessel">\n        pressure vessels\n       </a>\n       that make up the engine\xe2\x80\x94the pumps, pipes and combustion chambers involved. The lack of inlet duct and the use of dense liquid propellant allows the pressurisation system to be small and lightweight, whereas duct engines have to deal with air which has a density about one thousand times lower.\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable sortable">\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         <a href="/wiki/Jet_engine" title="Jet engine">\n          Jet\n         </a>\n </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/NK-33" title="NK-33">\n          NK-33\n         </a>\n         rocket engine\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NK33_20-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-NK33-20">\n           [20]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n        <td align="right">\n         1,222\n        </td>\n        <td align="right">\n </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Merlin_1D" title="Merlin 1D">\n          Merlin 1D\n         </a>\n         rocket engine, full-thrust version\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Merlin_1D_21-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-Merlin_1D-21">\n           [21]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n        <td
