  <td>\n         Hot water is stored in a tank at high temperature/pressure and turns to steam in nozzle\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Simple, fairly safe, under 200 seconds Isp\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Low overall performance due to heavy tank\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Solar_thermal">\n        Solar thermal\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rocket_engine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Solar thermal">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Solar_thermal_rocket" title="Solar thermal rocket">\n        Solar thermal rocket\n       </a>\n       would make use of solar power to directly heat\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reaction_mass" title="Reaction mass">\n        reaction mass\n       </a>\n       , and therefore does not require an electrical generator as most other forms of solar-powered propulsion do. A solar thermal rocket only has to carry the means of capturing solar energy, such as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Concentrating_solar_power" title="Concentrating solar power">\n        concentrators\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Mirror" title="Mirror">\n        mirrors\n       </a>\n       . The heated propellant is fed through a conventional rocket nozzle to produce thrust. The engine thrust is directly related to the surface area of the solar collector and to the local intensity of the solar radiation and inversely proportional to the\n       <i>\n        I\n       </i>\n       <sub>\n        sp\n       </sub>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable">\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         <b>\n          Type\n         </b>\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         <b>\n          Description\n         </b>\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         <b>\n          Advantages\n         </b>\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         <b>\n          Disadvantages\n         </b>\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         <a href="/wiki/Solar_thermal_rocket" title="Solar thermal rocket">\n          Solar thermal rocket\n         </a>\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         Propellant is heated by solar collector\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Simple design. Using hydrogen propellant, 900 seconds of\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Specific_Impulse" title="Specific Impulse">\n          <i>\n           I\n          </i>\n          <sub>\n           sp\n          </sub>\n         </a>\n         is comparable to Nuclear Thermal rocket, without the problems and complexity of controlling a fission reaction.\n         <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n          [\n          <i>\n           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n            <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2011)">\n             citation needed\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </i>\n          ]\n         </sup>\n         <p>\n          Ability to\n          <a href="/wiki/Solar_thermal_rocket#Proposed_solar-thermal_space_systems" title="Solar thermal rocket">\n           productively use\n          </a>\n          waste gaseous\n          <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen" title="Hydrogen">\n           hydrogen\n          </a>\n          \xe2\x80\x94an inevitable byproduct of long-term\n          <a href="/wiki/Liquid_hydrogen" title="Liquid hydrogen">\n           liquid hydrogen\n          </a>\n          storage in the\n          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radiative_heat_transfer" title="Radiative heat transfer">\n           radiative heat\n          </a>\n          environment of space\xe2\x80\x94for both\n          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orbital_stationkeeping" title="Orbital stationkeeping">\n           orbital stationkeeping\n          </a>\n          and\n          <a href="/wiki/Attitude_control" title="Attitude control">\n           attitude control\n          </a>\n          .\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aiaa20100902_39-0">\n           <a href="#cite_note-aiaa20100902-39">\n            [39]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </p>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Only useful once in space, as thrust is fairly low, but hydrogen has not been traditionally thought to be easily stored in space,\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aiaa20100902_39-1">\n          <a href="#cite_note-aiaa20100902-39">\n           [39]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         otherwise moderate/low\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Specific_Impulse" title="Specific Impulse">\n          <i>\n           I\n          </i>\n          <sub>\n           sp\n          </sub>\n         </a>\n         if higher\xe2\x80\x93molecular-mass propellants are used. Using higher\xe2\x80\x93molecular-weight propellants, for example water, lowers performance.\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Ion_thruster" title="Ion thruster">\n        Ion thruster\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Beamed_thermal">\n        Beamed thermal\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rocket_engine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Beamed thermal">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <table class="wikitable">\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         <b>\n          Type\n         </b>\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         <b>\n          Description\n         </b>\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         <b>\n          Advantages\n         </b>\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         <b>\n          Disadvantages\n         </b>\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         <a href="/wiki/Laser_propulsion" title="Laser propulsion">\n          light beam powered rocket\n         </a>\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         Propellant is heated by light beam (often laser) aimed at vehicle from a distance, either directly or indirectly via heat exchanger\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Simple in principle, in principle very high exhaust speeds can be achieved\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         ~1 MW of power per kg of payload is needed to achieve orbit, relatively high accelerations, lasers are blocked by clouds, fog, reflected laser light may be dangerous, pretty much needs hydrogen monopropellant for good performance which needs heavy tankage, some designs are limited to ~600 seconds due to reemission of light since propellant/heat exchanger gets white hot\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         <a href="/wiki/Beam-powered_propulsion" title="Beam-powered propulsion">\n          microwave beam powered rocket\n         </a>\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         Propellant is heated by microwave beam aimed at vehicle from a distance\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Specific_Impulse" title="Specific Impulse">\n          <i>\n           I\n          </i>\n          <sub>\n           sp\n          </sub>\n         </a>\n         is comparable to Nuclear Thermal rocket combined with T/W comparable to conventional rocket. While LH\n         <sub>\n          2\n         </sub>\n         propellant offers the highest I\n         <sub>\n          sp\n         </sub>\n         and rocket payload fraction, ammonia or methane are economically superior for earth-to-orbit rockets due to their particular combination of high density and I\n         <sub>\n          sp\n         </sub>\n         .\n         <a href="/wiki/Single-stage-to-orbit" title="Single-stage-to-orbit">\n          SSTO\n         </a>\n         operation is possible with these propellants even for small rockets, so there are no location, trajectory and shock constraints added by the rocket staging process. Microwaves are 10x-100x cheaper in $/Watt than lasers and have all-weather operation at frequencies below 10 GHz.\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         0.3-3 MW of power per kg of payload is needed to achieve orbit depending on the propellant,\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">\n          <a href="#cite_note-40">\n           [40]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         and this incurs infrastructure cost for the beam director plus related R&amp;D costs. Concepts operating in the millimeter-wave region have to contend with weather availability and high altitude beam director sites as well as effective transmitter diameters measuring 30-300 meters to propel a vehicle to LEO. Concepts operating in X-band or below must have effective transmitter diameters measured in kilometers to achieve a fine enough beam to follow a vehicle to LEO. The transmitters are too large to fit on mobile platforms and so microwave-powered rockets are constrained to launch near fixed beam director sites.\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Nuclear_thermal">\n        Nuclear thermal\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rocket_engine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Nuclear thermal">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <table class="wikitable">\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         <b>\n          Type\n         </b>\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         <b>\n          Description\n         </b>\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         <b>\n          Advantages\n         </b>\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         <b>\n          Disadvantages\n         </b>\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         <a href="/wiki/Radioisotope_rocket" title="Radioisotope rocket">\n          Radioisotope rocket/"Poodle thruster"\n         </a>\n         (radioactive decay energy)\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         Heat from radioactive decay is used to heat hydrogen\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         about 700\xe2\x80\x93800 seconds, almost no moving parts\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         low thrust/weight ratio.\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_thermal_rocket" title="Nuclear thermal rocket">\n          Nuclear thermal rocket\n         </a>\n         (nuclear fission energy)\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         propellant (typ. hydrogen) is passed through a nuclear reactor to heat to high temperature\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Specific_Impulse" title="Specific Impulse">\n          <i>\n           I\n          </i>\n          <sub>\n           sp\n          </sub>\n         </a>\n         can be high, perhaps 900 seconds or more, above unity thrust/weight ratio with some designs\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Maximum temperature is limited by materials technology, some radioactive particles can be present in exhaust in some designs, nuclear reactor shielding is heavy, unlikely to be permitted from surface of the Earth, thrust/weight ratio is not high.\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Nuclear">\n        Nuclear\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rocket_engine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Nuclear">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_propulsion" title="Nuclear propulsion">\n        Nuclear propulsion\n       </a>\n       includes a wide variety of\n       <a href="/wiki/Spacecraft_propulsion" title="Spacecraft propulsion">\n        propulsion\n       </a>\n       methods that use some form of\n       <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_reaction" title="Nuclear reaction">\n        nuclear reaction\n       </a>\n       as their primary power source. Various types of nuclear propulsion have been proposed, and some of them tested, for spacecraft applications:\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable">\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         <b>\n          Type\n         </b>\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         <b>\n          Description\n         </b>\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         <b>\n          Advantages\n         </b>\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         <b>\n          Disadvantages\n         </b>\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         <a href="/wiki/Gas_core_reactor_rocket" title="Gas core reactor rocket">\n          Gas core reactor rocket\n         </a>\n         (nuclear fission energy)\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         Nuclear reaction using a gaseous state fission reactor in intimate contact with propellant\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Very hot propellant, not limited by keeping reactor solid,\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Specific_Impulse" title="Specific Impulse">\n          <i>\n           I\n          </i>\n          <sub>\n           sp\n          </sub>\n         </a>\n         between 1,500 and 3,000 seconds but with very high thrust\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Difficulties in heating propellant without losing fissionables in exhaust, massive thermal issues particularly for nozzle/throat region, exhaust almost inherently highly radioactive. Nuclear lightbulb variants can contain fissionables, but cut\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Specific_Impulse" title="Specific Impulse">\n          <i>\n           I\n          </i>\n          <sub>\n           sp\n          </sub>\n         </a>\n         in half.\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         <a href="/wiki/Fission-fragment_rocket" title="Fission-fragment rocket">\n          Fission-fragment rocket\n         </a>\n         (nuclear fission energy)\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         Fission products are directly exhausted to give thrust\n        </td>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Theoretical only at this point.\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         <a href="/wiki/Fission_sail" title="Fission sail">\n          Fission sail\n         </a>\n         (nuclear fission energy)\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         A sail material is coated with fissionable material on one side\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         No moving parts, works in deep space\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Theoretical only at this point.\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_salt-water_rocket" title="Nuclear salt-water rocket">\n          Nuclear salt-water rocket\n         </a>\n         (nuclear fission energy)\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         Nuclear salts are held in solution, caused to react at nozzle\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Very high\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Specific_Impulse" title="Specific Impulse">\n          <i>\n           I\n          </i>\n          <sub>\n           sp\n          </sub>\n         </a>\n         , very high thrust\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Thermal issues in nozzle, propellant could be unstable, highly radioactive exhaust. Theoretical only at this point.\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_pulse_propulsion" title="Nuclear pulse propulsion">\n          Nuclear pulse propulsion\n         </a>\n         (exploding fission/fusion bombs)\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         Shaped nuclear bombs are detonated behind vehicle and blast is caught by a \'pusher plate\'\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Very high\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Specific_Impulse" title="Specific Impulse">\n          <i>\n           I\n          </i>\n          <sub>\n           sp\n          </sub>\n         </a>\n         , very high thrust/weight ratio, no show stoppers are known for this technology\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Never been tested, pusher plate may\n         <a href="/wiki/Spall" title="Spall">\n          throw off fragments\n         </a>\n         due to shock, minimum size for nuclear bombs is still pretty big, expensive at small scales, nuclear treaty issues, fallout when used below Earth\'s magnetosphere.\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antimatter_catalyzed_nuclear_pulse_propulsion" title="Antimatter catalyzed nuclear pulse propulsion">\n          Antimatter catalyzed nuclear pulse propulsion\n         </a>\n         (fission and/or fusion energy)\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         Nuclear pulse propulsion with antimatter assist for smaller bombs\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Smaller sized vehicle might be possible\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Containment of antimatter, production of antimatter in macroscopic quantities is not currently feasible. Theoretical only at this point.\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         <a href="/wiki/Fusion_rocket" title="Fusion rocket">\n          Fusion rocket\n         </a>\n         (nuclear fusion energy)\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         Fusion is used to heat propellant\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Very high exhaust velocity\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Largely beyond current state of the art.\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         <a href="/wiki/Antimatter_rocket" title="Antimatter rocket">\n          Antimatter rocket\n         </a>\n         (annihilation energy)\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         Antimatter annihilation heats propellant\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Extremely energetic, very high theoretical exhaust velocity\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Problems with antimatter production and handling; energy losses in\n         <a href="/wiki/Neutrino" title="Neutrino">\n          neutrinos\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Gamma_ray" title="Gamma ray">\n          gamma rays\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Muon" title="Muon">\n          muons\n         </a>\n         ; thermal issues. Theoretical only at this point\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="History_of_rocket_engines">\n        History of rocket engines\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rocket_engine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: History of rocket engines">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       According to the writings of the Roman\n       <a href="/wiki/Aulus_Gellius" title="Aulus Gellius">\n        Aulus Gellius\n       </a>\n       , in c. 400 BC, a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greek_people" title="Greek people">\n        Greek\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Pythagoreanism" title="Pythagoreanism">\n        Pythagorean\n       </a>\n       named\n       <a href="/wiki/Archytas" title="Archytas">\n        Archytas\n       </a>\n       , propelled a wooden bird along wires using steam.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">\n        <a href="#cite_note-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       However, it would not appear to have been powerful enough to take off under its own thrust.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Aeolipile" title="Aeolipile">\n         aeolipile\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       described in the first century BC (often known as\n       <i>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hero%27s_engine" title="Hero\'s engine">\n         Hero\'s engine\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ) essentially consists of a\n       <a href="/wiki/Steam_rocket" title="Steam rocket">\n        steam rocket\n       </a>\n       on a\n       <a href="/wiki/Bearing_(mechanical)" title="Bearing (mechanical)">\n        bearing\n       </a>\n       . It was created almost two millennia before the\n       <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">\n        Industrial Revolution\n       </a>\n       but the principles behind it were not well understood, and its full potential was not realised for a millennium.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The availability of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_powder" title="Black powder">\n        black powder\n       </a>\n       to propel projectiles was a precursor to the development of the first solid rocket. Ninth Century\n       <a href="/wiki/Chinese_people" title="Chinese people">\n        Chinese\n       </a>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taoist" title="Taoist">\n        Taoist\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Alchemy" title="Alchemy">\n        alchemists\n       </a>\n       discovered black powder in a search for the\n       <a href="/wiki/Elixir_of_life" title="Elixir of life">\n        elixir of life\n       </a>\n       ; this accidental discovery led to\n       <a href="/wiki/Fire_arrow" title="Fire arrow">\n        fire arrows\n       </a>\n       which were the first rocket engines to leave the ground.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       It is stated that "the reactive forces of incendiaries were probably not applied to the propulsion of projectiles prior to the 13th century". A turning point in rocket technology emerged with a short manuscript entitled\n       <i>\n        Liber Ignium ad Comburendos Hostes\n       </i>\n       (abbreviated as\n       <i>\n        The Book of Fires\n       </i>\n       ). The manuscript is composed of recipes for creating incendiary weapons from the mid-eighth to the end of the thirteenth centuries\xe2\x80\x94two of which are rockets. The first recipe calls for one part of colophonium and sulfur added to six parts of saltpeter (potassium nitrate) dissolved in laurel oil, then inserted into hollow wood and lit to "fly away suddenly to whatever place you wish and burn up everything". The second recipe combines one pound of sulfur, two pounds of charcoal, and six pounds of saltpeter\xe2\x80\x94all finely powdered on a marble slab. This powder mixture is packed firmly into a long and narrow case. The introduction of saltpeter into pyrotechnic mixtures connected the shift from hurled\n       <a href="/wiki/Greek_fire" title="Greek fire">\n        Greek fire\n       </a>\n       into self-propelled rocketry. .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">\n        <a href="#cite_note-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Articles and books on the subject of rocketry appeared increasingly from the fifteenth through seventeenth centuries. In the sixteenth century, German military engineer Conrad Haas (1509-1576) wrote a manuscript which introduced the construction to multi-staged rockets.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">\n        <a href="#cite_note-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Rocket engines were also brought in use by\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tippu_Sultan" title="Tippu Sultan">\n        Tippu Sultan\n       </a>\n       , the king of Mysore. These rockets could be of various sizes, but usually consisted of a tube of soft hammered iron about 8\xc2\xa0in (20\xc2\xa0cm) long and\n       <span class="frac nowrap">\n        1\n        <span class="visualhide">\n        </span>\n        <sup>\n         1\n        </sup>\n        \xe2\x81\x84\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n       </span>\n       \xe2\x80\x933\xc2\xa0in (3.8\xe2\x80\x937.6\xc2\xa0cm) diameter, closed at one end and strapped to a shaft of bamboo about 4\xc2\xa0ft (120\xc2\xa0cm) long. The iron tube acted as a combustion chamber and contained well packed black powder propellant. A rocket carrying about one pound of powder could travel almost 1,000 yards (910\xc2\xa0m). These \'rockets\', fitted with swords used to travel long distance, several meters above in air before coming down with swords edges facing the enemy. These rockets were used against British empire very effectively.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Slow development of this technology continued up to the later 19th century, when Russian\n       <a href="/wiki/Konstantin_Tsiolkovsky" title="Konstantin Tsiolkovsky">\n        Konstantin Tsiolkovsky\n       </a>\n       first wrote about\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liquid_rocket" title="Liquid rocket">\n        liquid-fueled rocket engines\n       </a>\n       . He was the first to develop the\n       <a href="/wiki/Tsiolkovsky_rocket_equation" title="Tsiolkovsky rocket equation">\n        Tsiolkovsky rocket equation\n       </a>\n       , though it was not published widely for some years.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The modern solid- and liquid-fueled engines became realities early in the 20th century, thanks to the American physicist\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Robert_Goddard_(scientist)" title="Robert Goddard (scientist)">\n        Robert Goddard\n       </a>\n       . Goddard was the first to use a\n       <a href="/wiki/De_Laval_nozzle" title="De Laval nozzle">\n        De Laval nozzle\n       </a>\n       on a solid-propellant (gunpowder) rocket engine, doubling the thrust and increasing the efficiency by a factor of about twenty-five. This was the birth of the modern rocket engine. He calculated from his independently-derived rocket equation that a reasonably sized rocket, using solid fuel, could place a one-pound payload on the Moon. He began to use liquid propellants in 1921 and was the first to launch, in 1926, a liquid-propellant rocket. Goddard pioneered the use of the De Laval nozzle, lightweight propellant tanks, thrust vectoring, the smoothly-throttled liquid fuel engine, regenerative cooling, and curtain cooling.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sutton_6-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Sutton-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :247\xe2\x80\x93266\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During the late 1930s, German scientists, such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Wernher_von_Braun" title="Wernher von Braun">\n        Wernher von Braun\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Hellmuth_Walter" title="Hellmuth Walter">\n        Hellmuth Walter\n       </a>\n       , investigated installing liquid-fueled rockets in military aircraft (\n       <a href="/wiki/Heinkel_He_112" title="Heinkel He 112">\n        Heinkel He 112\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Heinkel_He_111" title="Heinkel He 111">\n        He 111\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Heinkel_He_176" title="Heinkel He 176">\n        He 176\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Messerschmitt_Me_163" title="Messerschmitt Me 163">\n        Messerschmitt Me 163\n       </a>\n       ).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">\n        <a href="#cite_note-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The turbopump was first employed by German scientists in WWII. Until then cooling the nozzle had been problematic, and the\n       <a href="/wiki/V-2_rocket" title="V-2 rocket">\n        A4\n       </a>\n       ballistic missile used dilute alcohol for the fuel, which reduced the combustion temperature sufficiently.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Staged_combustion_cycle_(rocket)" title="Staged combustion cycle (rocket)">\n        Staged combustion\n       </a>\n       (\n       <i>\n        \xd0\x97\xd0\xb0\xd0\xbc\xd0\xba\xd0\xbd\xd1\x83\xd1\x82\xd0\xb0\xd1\x8f \xd1\x81\xd1\x85\xd0\xb5\xd0\xbc\xd0\xb0\n       </i>\n       ) was first proposed by\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aleksei_Mihailovich_Isaev" title="Aleksei Mihailovich Isaev">\n        Alexey Isaev\n       </a>\n       in 1949. The first staged combustion engine was the S1.5400 used in the Soviet planetary rocket, designed by Melnikov, a former assistant to Isaev.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sutton_6-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Sutton-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       About the same time (1959),\n       <a href="/wiki/Nikolai_Dmitriyevich_Kuznetsov" title="Nikolai Dmitriyevich Kuznetsov">\n        Nikolai Kuznetsov\n       </a>\n       began work on the closed cycle engine\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=NK-9&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="NK-9 (page does not exist)">\n        NK-9\n       </a>\n       for Korolev\'s orbital ICBM, GR-1. Kuznetsov later evolved that design into the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NK-15" title="NK-15">\n        NK-15\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/NK-33" title="NK-33">\n        NK-33\n       </a>\n       engines for the unsuccessful Lunar\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/N1_rocket" title="N1 rocket">\n        N1 rocket\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the West, the first laboratory staged-combustion test engine was built in Germany in 1963, by\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ludwig_Boelkow" title="Ludwig Boelkow">\n        Ludwig Boelkow\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Hydrogen peroxide / kerosene fueled engines such as the British\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gamma_(Rocket_engine)" title="Gamma (Rocket engine)">\n        Gamma\n       </a>\n       of the 1950s used a closed-cycle process (arguably not\n       <i>\n        staged combustion\n       </i>\n       , but that\'s mostly a question of semantics) by catalytically decomposing the peroxide to drive turbines\n       <i>\n        before\n       </i>\n       combustion with the kerosene in the combustion chamber proper. This gave the efficiency advantages of staged combustion, whilst avoiding the major engineering problems.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Liquid hydrogen engines were first successfully developed in America, the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RL-10" title="RL-10">\n        RL-10\n       </a>\n       engine first flew in 1962. Hydrogen engines were used as part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">\n        Apollo program\n       </a>\n       ; the liquid hydrogen fuel giving a rather lower stage mass and thus reducing the overall size and cost of the vehicle.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">\n        See also\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rocket_engine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: See also">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Comparison_of_orbital_rocket_engines" title="Comparison of orbital rocket engines">\n         Comparison of orbital rocket engines\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Jet_damping" title="Jet damping">\n         Jet damping\n        </a>\n        an effect of the exhaust jet of a rocket that tends to slow a vehicle\'s rotation speed\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Laser_propulsion" title="Laser propulsion">\n         Laser propulsion\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Model_rocket_motor_classification" title="Model rocket motor classification">\n         Model rocket motor classification\n        </a>\n        lettered engines\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/NERVA" title="NERVA">\n         NERVA\n        </a>\n        -\n        <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">\n         NASA\n        </a>\n        \'s Nuclear Energy for Rocket Vehicle Applications, a US nuclear thermal rocket programme\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Photon_rocket" title="Photon rocket">\n         Photon rocket\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Project_Prometheus" title="Project Prometheus">\n         Project Prometheus\n        </a>\n        , NASA development of nuclear propulsion for long-duration spaceflight, begun in 2003\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="References">\n        References\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span
